                <h3 class="c-article__sub-heading">Competing interests</h3>
                <p>The authors declare no competing financial interests.</p>
              
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec15" data-title="Extended data figures and tables"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec15-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec15">Extended data figures and tables</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec15-content"><div data-test="supplementary-info"><div id="figshareContainer" class="c-article-figshare-container" data-test="figshare-container"></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig4"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature15714/figures/4" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature15714/MediaObjects/41586_2015_Article_BFnature15714_Fig4_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 1 Summary of the <i>Oropetium</i> genome assembly statistics.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Histogram of length distribution of raw P6C4 chemistry PacBio reads. The mean read length of the raw reads is 12,872 bp, and the N50 is 16,485 bp. <b>b</b>, Genome size estimation using <i>k</i>-mer distribution. <i>K</i>-mer distribution of unassembled <i>Oropetium</i> Illumina WGS reads. <i>K</i>-mer frequency displays a unimodal curve indicating a low rate of heterozygosity in the <i>Oropetium</i> genome. Frequency distribution suggests a genome size of ~245 Mb, consistent with flow-cytometry-based estimations. <b>c</b>, SMRT sequencing raw read, preassembly and assembly statistics. <b>d</b>, <b>e</b>, The distribution of the contig N50 length (<b>d</b>) and scaffold N50 length (<b>e</b>) of all published plant genomes is plotted. The average contig N50 length for published plant genomes is ~50 kb compared to 2.4 Mb for <i>Oropetium</i>. <b>f</b>, <b>g</b>, Repeat density (as a function of percentage repeats) (<b>f</b>) and GC content (<b>g</b>) are plotted at a scaled position along each contig. Each contig was divided into 5,000 sliding windows with each window representing 0.02% of the contig length and the averages of each scaled sliding window are plotted. Repeat content and GC content do not vary at the ends of contigs. <b>h</b>, Estimated accuracy of SMRT PacBio assembly and within-genome heterozygosity. <b>i</b>, Comparison of HGAP Falcon and MHAP PacBio assemblers.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig5"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature15714/figures/5" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature15714/MediaObjects/41586_2015_Article_BFnature15714_Fig5_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 2 PacBio sequencing and assembly completely resolves the <i>Oropetium</i> centromeres.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, The <i>Oropetium</i> centromere repeat base is 155 bp (red arrow), whereas they are also found in dimer (310 bp, grey arrow), trimer (465 bp, black arrow) and tetramer (620 bp, white arrow) form. <b>b</b>, As the copy number of a repeat increases, the match identity between monomers in the repeat decreases. <b>c</b>, The inverted repeat structure of the entire centromere on contig028 with a 60 kb spacer (blue box); arrows are as in <b>a</b>. <b>d</b>, Consensus 155 bp centromere monomer. <b>e</b>, Integrated genome browser view of centromere repeat, LTRs and predicted genes on contig028.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig6"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature15714/figures/6" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature15714/MediaObjects/41586_2015_Article_BFnature15714_Fig6_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 3 Macrosynteny patterns and comparative genomics between the grasses.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>–<b>e</b>, Macrosynteny of <i>Oropetium</i> versus <i>Oropetium</i> (<b>a</b>); <i>Oropetium</i> versus <i>Brachypodium</i> (<b>b</b>); <i>Oropetium</i> versus rice (<b>c</b>); <i>Oropetium</i> versus <i>Setaria</i> (<b>d</b>); and <i>Oropetium</i> versus <i>Sorghum</i> (<b>e</b>). <b>f</b>, Genome compaction in <i>Oropetium</i> compared to related grass genomes. Syntenic block span is based on regions that show conserved synteny across all five genomes. Syntenic gene and coding DNA sequences span is based on 13,683 genes that are retained as genes in orthologous locations across all five genomes. The ratio compared to <i>Oropetium</i> is given in brackets.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig7"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature15714/figures/7" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature15714/MediaObjects/41586_2015_Article_BFnature15714_Fig7_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 4 Expansion of intragenic and pericentric regions in <i>Sorghum</i> compared to <i>Oropetium</i>.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, A GEvo sequence similarity graphic of an <i>Oropetium</i> gene (upper) and its orthologous <i>Sorghum</i> gene (lower). Blast hits (high-scoring segment pairs) are denoted by red rectangles, and syntenic hits are connected by a red line. The green rectangles on the model line of <i>Sorghum</i> are conserved noncoding sequences (CNS) computed between <i>Sorghum</i> and rice; the expanse of CNS coverage defines ‘gene space’. Within the oval are three CNS that may be spatially constrained. The expanded interspersed sequences are annotated at the bottom in black. <b>b</b>, Pericentric region expansion in <i>Sorghum</i> compared to <i>Oropetium</i>. A syntenic dot plot of the <i>Sorghum</i> and <i>Oropetium</i> genomes is plotted. <i>Oropetium</i> contigs are ordered based on synteny with <i>Sorghum</i>. Hits are coloured based on K<sub>s</sub> divergence, with purple blocks corresponding to 1:1 orthologous regions and other colours corresponding to retained genes from the rho and sigma WGDs. Pericentric regions in <i>Sorghum</i> have few syntenic matches to <i>Oropetium</i>, suggesting that much of the expansion occurred in pericentric regions.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig8"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature15714/figures/8" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature15714/MediaObjects/41586_2015_Article_BFnature15714_Fig8_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 5 Assembly improvement using a BioNano-based genome map from the Irys system.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Distribution of molecule size for raw single-molecule genome mapping data. Size of single molecules in nanochannel arrays is plotted. <b>b</b>, Integration of the genome map with the genome assembly. Overlap between the PacBio-based contigs and the genome map. Each line shows a single PacBio contig in green; genome maps are shown in light blue.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig9"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" statistics for tandem duplicated genes.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Tandem duplicated genes in the metabolic network are shown in pink. <b>b</b>, Distribution of shared neighbours. <b>c</b>, The average number of neighbours.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item" data-test="supp-item"><div             <aside><div class="c-article-editorial-summary__container" data-component-show-more="true" id="editorial-summary"><section><h1 class="c-article-editorial-summary__title u-h3">Editorial Summary</h1><h2 class="c-article-editorial-summary__article-title">A genomic model for drought tolerance</h2><div class="c-article-editorial-summary__content c-article-editorial-summary__content--less"><p><i>Oropetium thomaeum</i> is a resurrection plant that can endure extreme water stress through desiccation to complete dryness whilst retaining the ability to revive when water is available, providing a model for drought tolerance. These authors report whole-genome sequencing and assembly of the <i>O. thomaeum</i> genome, using only single-molecule real-time (SMRT) long-read sequencing. Understanding the genomic mechanisms of extreme desiccation tolerance in resurrection plants such as <i>Oropetium</i> may provide targets for engineering drought and stress tolerance in crop plants.</p></div></section></div></aside>
